# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Your Task

Perfect! I've successfully completed the analysis and created the answer file. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Summary

I found the Go source files in grafana/grafana that implement the alerting evaluation scheduler tick and detect when evaluation cycles overrun their time budget:

### Key Files:
1. **`pkg/services/ngalert/schedule/schedule.go`** - Main scheduler that processes ticks and logs the warning
2. **`pkg/services/ngalert/schedule/alert_rule.go`** - Rule evaluation routine that detects overrun
3. **`pkg/services/ngalert/schedule/ticker/ticker.go`** - Ticker that emits regular ticks
4. **`pkg/services/ngalert/eval/eval.go`** - Applies evaluation timeout

### How It Works:
The scheduler runs a periodic loop via `schedulePeriodic()` that receives ticks from the ticker. For each tick, `processTick()` schedules alert rules for evaluation. The `runJobFn()` method sends evaluation signals to rule routines via the `Eval()` method.

The key timeout detection happens in `alert_rule.Eval()` (line 206): it performs a non-blocking read of the evaluation channel. If there's already a pending evaluation (the rule hasn't finished processing the previous tick), this pending evaluation is captured as `droppedMsg`. When this happens, `runJobFn()` logs the warning: **"Tick dropped because alert rule evaluation is too slow"** (line 442).

The evaluation timeout budget is enforced in `eval.EvaluateRaw()` which uses `context.WithTimeout()` with the configured `EvaluationTimeout` to create a deadline for the evaluation execution.

The answer has been written to `/workspace/answer.json` with all relevant files, symbols, and execution chain documented.

This package is responsible for managing the evaluation\\n24: of alert rules including checking for new alert rules and stopping the evaluation of deleted alert rules.\\n25: \\n26: The scheduler runs at a fixed interval, called its heartbeat, in which it does a number of tasks:\\n27: \\n28: 1. Send an `*evaluation` event to the goroutine for each alert rule if its interval has elapsed\\n31: 4. Stop the goroutines for all alert rules that have been deleted since the last heartbeat\\n32: \\n33: The function that evaluates each alert rule is called `run`. It waits for an `*evaluation` event (sent each\\n34: interval seconds elapsed and is configurable per alert rule) and then evaluates the alert rule. To ensure that the\\n35: ... The `T.run()` method (line 55) implements the ticker that emits ticks on interval marks at predictable times.\\n\\n## Evaluation Cycle Overrun Detection and Logging\\nThe warning message \\\"Tick dropped because alert rule evaluation is too slow\\\" is logged in `pkg/services/ngalert/schedule/schedule.go` in the `runJobFn()` method (lines 441-445). This method sends evaluation signals to alert rule routines and checks if any ticks were dropped.\\n\\nThe actual timeout detection happens in `pkg/services/ngalert/schedule/alert_rule.go` in the `Eval()` method (line 206). This method implements a non-blocking check of the evaluation channel. If a new evaluation arrives while the previous one is still in progress (still pending in the channel), the previous evaluation is captured as `droppedMsg` and returned to the caller. This indicates that the evaluation cycle has overrun its time budget.\\n\\nThe alert rule evaluation loop is in the `Run()` method (line 251), which processes evaluation signals. The actual evaluation execution happens in the `evaluate()` method (line 400).\\n\\n## Evaluation Timeout Application\\nThe evaluation timeout budget is applied in `pkg/services/ngalert/eval/eval.go` in the `EvaluateRaw()` method (lines 74-77).
